GT Equivalence Verification (BPG4)

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

**GT expression:**
`0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

Expanding the first term:
`0.1728*P - 0.1728*P┬▓/48.55 + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`
`= -0.003558*P┬▓ + 0.1728*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(1.407 - 1.524*P))`

Key observations:
- The GT depends only on P (not on t!)
- It has a P┬▓ term, a P term, and a sigmoid-like term involving P: `P/(1 + exp(a - b*P))`

Since the GT is independent of t, any candidate with t-dependent terms must have those terms' coefficients set to 0.

Let me look for candidates that, after setting t-dependent terms to zero, can produce `c0*P┬▓ + c1*P + f(P)` where f(P) involves a sigmoid or similar nonlinearity in P.

**Candidate 13:** `P┬│*c0/(P+c1) + P┬▓*c2/(P+c1) + P┬▓*c3/(P+c1) + P*c4/(P+c1) + P*c5/(P+c1) + c6/(P+c1) + c7/(P+c1)`
This simplifies to `(c0*P┬│ + (c2+c3)*P┬▓ + (c4+c5)*P + (c6+c7))/(P+c1)`. This is a rational function, not a sigmoid. Won't match.

**Candidate 24:** `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*exp(c3/(c4+t)) + c5/(P+c6)`
Setting t-terms: the exp term becomes a constant when c3=0: `c2*exp(0) = c2`. So: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c5/(P+c6)`. This is rational in P, not sigmoid. Won't match.

**Candidate 42:** `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3) + c4*exp(c5/(c6+t))`
With c5=0: constant. So `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*P/(P+c3) + c4`. This gives rational terms, not sigmoid.

Now let me look for candidates with `exp(P*c)` type terms:

**Candidate 19:** `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*t*exp(c3*t) + c4*exp(P*c5 + c6*t) + c7*t/PтБ╡`
Setting t-terms to 0 (c2=0, c7=0, but c4*exp(P*c5+c6*t) тАФ need c6=0): `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c4*exp(P*c5)`. This is exp(P), not sigmoid.

**Candidate 22:** `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*t/(c3+t┬▓) + c4*exp(c5/(c6+t)) + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9)+1)`
Setting t-dependent terms to constants (c2=0, c5=0): `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c4 + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9)+1)`

Now, `log(c8*exp(P*c9)+1)`. Note that `P/(1+exp(a-bP))` is not directly a log-sum-exp. But the derivative of log(exp(x)+1) is sigmoid. These aren't equivalent.

**Candidate 34:** `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*exp(c3/(c4+t)) + c5*exp(P*c6+c7*t) + c8/(P+c9)`
With c3=0, c7=0: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2 + c5*exp(P*c6) + c8/(P+c9)`. Still not sigmoid.

The GT has `P/(1+exp(f(P)))` which is `P*sigmoid(g(P))`. This is a very specific nonlinear function of P. None of the candidates have a sigmoid function, a `1/(1+exp(...))` structure, or `P/(c+exp(P))` type terms.

After careful review of all 50 candidates, none can reproduce the sigmoid-type term `P/(1+exp(a+bP))` from the GT. The candidates use exp, log, sin, tanh, power functions, and rational functions, but none combine them in a way that produces `P*sigmoid(P)`.

Wait тАФ **Candidate 20** has `tanh`: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3 + c4*tanh(c5*t+c6) + c7*t*exp(c8*t)`. Setting t-terms to 0: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c3*P^c2 + c4*tanh(c6)`. The tanh becomes constant. No match.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))

I need to analyze each candidate to determine if it can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

Simplifying GT:
- First term: `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P┬▓` (a linear + quadratic in P)
- Second term: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))` (a sigmoidal term in P)

The GT is a function of **P only** (no t dependence). This is crucial.

Key observations:
1. GT has NO dependence on t
2. GT has terms: `c*P┬▓`, `c*P`, and `c*P/(1 + exp(a*P + b))` тАФ a logistic/sigmoid term

For candidates with t-dependence, I can only eliminate t terms by setting their coefficients to 0. Let me check each candidate.

For candidates where t can be zeroed out, I need the remaining P-dependent terms to match GT's structure: quadratic in P plus a sigmoid-like term in P.

The sigmoid term `P/(1 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))` is critical. This cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, simple exponentials, logarithms, or trigonometric functions of P alone.

Let me identify which candidates can produce a sigmoid-like term `P/(1+exp(aP+b))`:

**Candidates with exp(something involving P):**
- Candidate 7: `exp(P^c6 * c7)` тАФ if c6=1, this is `exp(c7*P)`, could potentially work
- Candidate 14: `exp(P^c7 * c8)` тАФ similar
- Candidate 19: `exp(P*c5 + c6*t)` тАФ set c6=0, gives `exp(c5*P)`
- Candidate 21: `exp(P*c8 + c9*t)` тАФ set c9=0, gives `exp(c8*P)`
- Candidate 22: `log(c8*exp(P*c9) + 1)` тАФ this is a softplus! Could this work?

- Candidate 34: `exp(P*c6 + c7*t)` тАФ set c7=0

- Candidate 44: `exp(P*c5)` тАФ exponential in P
- Candidate 47: `exp(P^c8 * c9)` тАФ similar

Now, the GT sigmoid term is `P/(1 + exp(aP+b))`. None of these candidates have the structure `P/(1 + exp(...))`. They have bare `exp(...)` terms or `log(exp(...)+1)` terms.

Let me check Candidate 22 more carefully:
`P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c2*t/(c3+t┬▓) + c4*exp(c5/(c6+t)) + c7*log(c8*exp(P*c9) + 1)`

Setting t-terms to 0 (c2=0, c4=0): `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + c7*log(c8*exp(c9*P) + 1)`

The softplus `log(c8*exp(c9*P) + 1)` is NOT the same as `P/(1+exp(aP+b))`. These are fundamentally different functions.

Let me check Candidate 42: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3) + c4*exp(c5/(c6+t))`
Setting c4=0: `P┬▓*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P+c3)` тАФ this is rational in P, not sigmoid.
